# CLAIM 5: County Defense Rebuttal

## Legal Elements (Rebuttal of Anticipated County Defenses)
- **A-Rebut Zoning Power**: County exceeded authority / state preemption defeats zoning defense
- **B-Rebut Health/Safety Pretext**: Health/safety justification was pretextual / politically motivated
- **C-Rebut No Vested Rights**: Evidence establishing vested/prior rights county denies
- **D-Rebut No Taking**: Evidence rebutting county claim no taking occurred

---
# PART 1: HIGH INTEREST DOCUMENTS
*These documents contain the strongest evidence. Full text included for attorney review.*

Chloe Morroni

cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend Canyon
Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to begin the process to
amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in forestry and
recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is issuing the following
statement:
Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today. The message from
Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the Council, my planning staff, and the
District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the outpouring of public concern about proposed
extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be allowed by
County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious areas, especially as
we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and
safeguard our canyon areas for today and future generations.

###
For those unable to attend the meeting this morning at 9:30 a.m., a livestream is available on the County Council’s
Facebook page and the meeting agenda/attachments are located here.

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
Office of Regional Development
Tel. 385-479-2086
TTY 7-1-1
jcarroll@slco.org
Twitter: @jordanec & @slcoregionaldev
Facebook: Salt Lake County Regional Development

so SALT

LAKE
I- I COUNTY
EGIQNAL DEvELOPAAENit

Parleys Canyon
Emily Pulver <epulver14@gmail.com>
To: juliecarter@utah.gov

Sun, Jan 16, 2022 at 8:21 AM

Julie,
I am writing with my concerns about the proposed quarry mine in Parleys Canyon. We have a family
cabin in Mt. Aire and know other friends and family members that also have cabins there. It is a
beautiful spot we love to enjoy. Not only do we enjoy it but thousands of other people do as well.
That area is used for a lot of recreation by many people. It's also used by thousands each day for
transportation.
There are also concerns impacting wildlife, water and air quality, and traffic, to name a few. Many
people come from all over the world to see this area of Utah and it would be a shame to cloud the
beauty and accessibility with something like this proposed open limestone quarry.
I am sure you are aware of these negative effects so my main purpose in this email is to provide you
with one more family who has worries and concerns, not only for ourselves and how it impacts just
us, but for the community and all the people that it would negatively impact.
Thank you for your time and consideration,
Emily Pulver

The actions taken by the Salt Lake City Council today demonstrate disrespect for private property rights. This ordinance is blatantly
contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit

Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. Thus, it is illegal. We believe that it is not the County’s conscious intention to disobey state
law.
More alarming, the attorney for Tree Farm LLC, Brent Bateman, has sought numerous times to engage with Salt Lake County. With the
exception of dismissive emails from one county attorney, he was largely ignored.
Sadly, This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only the potential mine owner but of many others.
In the past decade, Utah’s population has grown at the fastest rate in the country, adding more than half a million residents in the last
ten years. With annual per-capita aggregate demand of around 10 tons, the rapidly growing Salt Lake City area will require 258 million
tons of various aggregates over the next 20 years. Failing to develop new, local aggregate sources will have serious consequences on
the environment and economy. Already-soaring housing and infrastructure costs will increase. Quality of life will diminish.
Additionally, this process has sadly shed a light on another serious issue: the attempt by privileged individuals in our state to

### SLCo003164 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

SLC_5827020.1


```

To whom it may concern:
On January 26, 2022, the Division of Oil, Gas and Mining (Division) received an Amended Notice of Intention
to Commence Large Mining Operations (Notice) for the 1-80 South Quarry (formally Silver Mine by Tree Farms
LLC). This amendment updates contact information to the new operator Granite Construction. Please be aware
that because this plan is not approved, the Division cannot approve this amendment.
There are still several outstanding deficiencies from the last review that need to be address prior to approval.
Therefore, the Division is returning this amendment. With any new responses or amendment please make sure
that this amendment is incorporated into the plan and that Granite Construction signs future submittals including
the mine signature page.
All future correspondence should reference M/035/0054. Thank you for your help in keeping this permit current.
Sincerely,

John Rogers

### SLCo003588 — State of Utah
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* mining and extracting critical infrastructure materials from various properties, owned by

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
State of Utah
Department of Commerce
SPENCER J. COX
Governor
DIEDRE M. HENDERSON
Lieutenant Governor

OFFICE OF THE PROPERTY RIGHTS OMBUDSMAN
MARGARET W. BUSSE
Executive Director

JORDAN S. CULLIMORE
Division Director, Office of the Property Rights Ombudsman

March 23, 2022

Rashelle Hobbs, City Recorder
Salt Lake County
2001 South State St. N1-600
Salt Lake City, Utah 84190

via email

RE: Mediation/Arbitration Request: Tree Farm, LLC
Property Address: 4402 East I-80 (Parley’s Canyon)
Dear Ms. Hobbs:
Attached please find a request for mediation that the Office of the Property Rights
Ombudsman (the “Office”) has received from Brent N. Bateman, on behalf of Tree Farm,
LLC (“Tree Farm”). The issue relates to action by Salt Lake County (“SLCO”). The Office
has reviewed the request and believes that it raises issues that may be appropriate for
mediation and/or arbitration under Utah statute. (See Utah Code § 13-43-204.)
According to the information we have received, Mr. Bateman indicates that Tree Farm is
mining and extracting critical infrastructure materials from various properties, owned by
Tree Farm, in Parley’s Canyon. Mr. Bateman claims SLCO is considering and has recently
passed zoning legislation to restrict further mining and extraction. Mr. Bateman asserts
that the County’s actions amount to a regulatory taking of his client’s property without
compensation. Tree Farm is seeking mediation to resolve this dispute.
We would like to proceed to have an initial conversation on the matter as soon as possible
to gather the perspectives of the other parties involved. In the interim, please consider
the following issues and respond if necessary.
* Are the facts as alleged true?
* Is there a chance to settle this matter without formal arbitration?
* Are there reasons that you believe this matter is not ripe for review?

160 East 300 South, PO Box 146702, Salt Lake City, UT 84114-6702• telephone (801) 530-6391 • propertyrights.utah.gov

Rashelle Hobbs
March 23, 2022
Page 2 of 2
* Is this dispute, or part of it, beyond the scope of this Office’s right to provide for
mediation or arbitration under the statute?
* Is the matter inappropriate for mediation or arbitration based on some other
factors?
Our Office would be eager to assist in any meaningful way with efforts to resolve the
matter in the most informal and expeditious manner possible, so long as this does not
result in unreasonable delay or other unfairness.
The attorneys in the Office are available to serve as the arbitrator in this matter. We are
also willing to assist as mediators if we can resolve the issues without arbitration. If
requested, a need for remote mediation through video conferencing can be
accommodated.
Thank you for your attention to this matter. Please advise me of any questions or
suggestions you have.
Sincerely,

Jordan S. Cullimore
Lead Attorney
Office of the Property Rights Ombudsman
Att:
cc (via email):

Brent N. Bateman, Esq.
Zachary D. Shaw, Esq.

### SLCo003684 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

SLC_5827020.1


```

County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.

### SLCo003686 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
SIM GILL

April 7, 2022
Via email – jcullimore@utah.gov
Utah Office of the Property Rights Ombudsman
Attn: Jordan Cullimore
Re: Tree Farm Request for Mediation
Dear Jordan:
As a follow up to our conversation last week, I write to address the issues raised by Tree Farm, LLC (TF)
in its letter and request for mediation (Request) filed with your office. In the Request, TF asserts that a
proposed amendment to the Salt Lake County zoning code has already imposed a regulatory taking on
TF. Then, based on the County’s proposed legislative amendments to its land use code, TF asserts that it
is entitled to just compensation from Salt Lake County. These assertions are not supported by the law.
Utah Code § 13-43-204 provides that the Ombudsman’s office can mediate disputes involving takings or
eminent domain issues. However, subsection (3)(b) of this section provides that mediation is not
appropriate if, in the opinion of the Property Rights Ombudsman, the issues are not ripe for review, no
cause of action exists (assuming the alleged facts are true), all issues raised are beyond the scope of the
Ombudsman’s statutory duty to review, or the mediation is otherwise not appropriate. For the following
reasons, mediation at this time is not appropriate under this statute.
In his letter, Mr. Bateman asserts that the County is prohibited from adopting or amending ordinances that
prohibit operations that remove “sand, gravel, and rock aggregate,” which are critical infrastructure
materials as defined by Utah Code §§ 17-27a-1001 & 17-41-101. As grounds, Mr. Bateman cited Utah
Code § 17-41-406(6), which limits the County’s ability to amend its existing land use ordinances to
prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical infrastructure materials operations. However, the
proposed amendments do not include any reference to critical infrastructure materials or critical
infrastructure materials operations, as defined by those statutes. As such, the proposed changes do not
conflict with Utah Code § 17-41-406, and the County is legally entitled to move forward with the
proposed amendments as currently drafted if the County elects to do so. As a point of information,
following the public hearing on April 5, 2022, the County Council voted unanimously to advance the
amendments, and did so based on unanimous public comment in support. The proposed amendments are
enclosed with this letter.
Second, TF claims that because Salt Lake County has initiated proceedings to amend its Forest Recreation
(FR)and Foothills Canyons Overlay Zone (FCOZ) zoning regulations to eliminate “mineral extraction” as
a conditional use within those zones, TF purportedly has suffered a regulatory taking. However, a
regulatory taking claim is not ripe until a government entity has issued a “fina
... [truncated — full text is 4415 characters]
```

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend Canyon
Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction

SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to begin the process to
amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in forestry and
recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is issuing the following
statement:
Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today. The message from
Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the Council, my planning staff, and the
District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the outpouring of public concern about proposed
extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be allowed by
County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious areas, especially as
we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and
safeguard our canyon areas for today and future generations.

### SLCo005710 — Proposed mining in Parley's Canyon
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* slows traffic to a crawl. A fleet of heavy gravel trucks, which will be needed to haul gravel up and down the

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: Bill Hanson <william.f.hanson@gmail.com>
To: LLStringham@slco.org, RSnelgrove@slco.org, JBradley@slco.org, DHTheodore@slco.org
Subject: Proposed mining in Parley's Canyon
Date: Mon, 04 Apr 2022 12:09:14 -0600
Importance: Normal

My name is William (Bill) F. Hanson. I've lived in Salt Lake County all my life, and have traveled up and down
Parleys Canyon countless times. I personally know Jim Bradley, although I haven't seen him for some time, and
Dea Theordore, a neighbor of mine. I think both can vouch that I'm not unreasonable. I've hiked all over the
Wasatch Range, and, even though I'm an old guy, still do so. The Wasatch Range is a great treasure that should
not be damaged by a mine in Parley's Canyon. These are some of the many reasons why.
1. Parley's Canyon is the primary means by which eastbound and westbound traffic enters and leaves the Salt
Lake Valley. As we all know, it's a lovely green in the Spring and Summer, yellow and red in the Fall, and white
in the Winter. It's a beautiful canyon that we all love and enjoy and an impressive way to enter and exit the Salt
Lake Valley. A huge strip-mine scar on its south side would irretrievably damage its beauty, all because some
guy wants to make lots of money at the expense of those of us who treasure it and live in the Salt Lake Valley.
2. As we who live in the Salt Lake Valley know, Winter inversions plague our air quality. And, even in other
seasons, the Salt Lake Valley's air quality can rapidly deteriorate. A huge gravel strip mine in Parley's Canyon,
together with its heavy machinery and gravel-hauling trucks, would, in my view, drastically exacerbate the
Valley's air quality, particularly in the Winter months, as strong winds typically blow down the Canyon. Will the
owner of the mine compensate those who suffer from the resulting dirty air and pay for the measures to clean it?
3. Parley's Canyon is, as a major east-west interstate traffic artery, well-traveled. As we know, it sometimes
suffers from heavily-congested heavy traffic, particularly during rush-hour times and when a vehicular accident
slows traffic to a crawl. A fleet of heavy gravel trucks, which will be needed to haul gravel up and down the
canyon from the proposed mine, will vastly exacerbate traffic congestion in the canyon. Moreover, those trucks
will, unless meticulously sealed, will spew gravel over other vehicles on the road. Will the owner of the
proposed mine willingly cover damage to other vehicles resulting from loose gravel? And, the constant use of
heavy trucks will cause the Parley's Canyon road to deteriorate much sooner than it otherwise would. Will the
owner of the proposed mine pay additional highway taxes commensurate with that deterioration? .
4. We've all seen what has happened to what used to be the Point of the Mountain. Heavy gravel mining there
has leveled the western part of it to the extent that there's no point left. Moreover, on windy days, gravel dust
from the mine can cover both the Inte
... [truncated — full text is 3658 characters]
```

### SLCo006122 — Date:
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

Chloe Morroni

cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend Canyon
Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to begin the process to
amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in forestry and
recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is issuing the following
statement:
Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today. The message from
Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the Council, my planning staff, and the
District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the outpouring of public concern about proposed
extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be allowed by
County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious areas, especially as
we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and
safeguard our canyon areas for today and future generations.

###
For those unable to attend the meeting this morning at 9:30 a.m., a livestream is available on the County Council’s
Facebook page and the meeting agenda/attachments are located here.

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
Office of Regional Development

jcarroll@slco.org

Facebook: Salt Lake County Regional Development

### SLCo006252 — December 10, 2021
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

> *Key Quote:* or Wilson is

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
December 10, 2021
Contact:

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
jcarroll@slco.org
(385) 479-2086

Chloe Morroni
Communications Director
cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend
Canyon Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to
begin the process to amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing
as a conditional use in forestry and recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is
issuing the following statement:

Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today.
The message from Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the
Council, my planning staff, and the District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the
outpouring of public concern about proposed extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be
allowed by County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious
areas, especially as we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my
administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and safeguard our canyon areas for today and future
generations.

### SLCo007444 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

law.

exception of dismissive emails from one county attorney, he was largely ignored.
Sadly, This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only the potential mine owner but of many others.
In the past decade, Utah’s population has grown at the fastest rate in the country, adding more than half a million residents in the last
ten years. With annual per-capita aggregate demand of around 10 tons, the rapidly growing Salt Lake City area will require 258 million
tons of various aggregates over the next 20 years. Failing to develop new, local aggregate sources will have serious consequences on
the environment and economy. Already-soaring housing and infrastructure costs will increase. Quality of life will diminish.

SALT LAKE COUNTY
County Council
Meeting Agenda
Tuesday, February 1, 2022

4:00 PM

2001 So. State Street
Salt Lake City, UT 84114
(385) 468-7500 TTY 711

Council Chambers, N1-110

Upon request and with three working days’ notice, Salt Lake County will provide free auxiliary
aids and services to qualified individuals (including sign language interpreters, alternative formats,
etc.). For assistance, please call (385) 468-7500 – TTY 711.
Members of the Council may participate electronically. Meetings may be closed for reasons
allowed by statute. Motions relating to any of the items listed below, including final action, may
be taken.
During the current phase of COVID-19 response and recovery, members of the public may attend
the Council’s meetings in person on a limited basis. Consistent with a directive issued by Salt
Lake County Mayor Jennifer Wilson on August 30, 2021, everyone who enters the Salt Lake
County Government Center is required to wear a face covering, regardless of vaccination status. A
copy of Mayor Wilson’s email can be viewed at https://slco.org/council/agendas/. Members of the
public may also participate in Council meetings electronically as described below.

Page 1 of 8

County Council

Meeting Agenda

February 1, 2022

This meeting will be simulcast electronically via Webex Events. Agendas, audio
live-streams and recordings, and meeting minutes can be accessed at slco.legistar.com. The
Council will also broadcast live-streams of its meetings on Facebook Live, which may be
accessed at http://www.facebook.com/slcocouncil/, and through Cisco Webex, which may
be accessed at:
https://slco.webex.com/slco/onstage/g.php?MTID=e978ceeb80941036b21740906fe754ee7
Individuals wishing to comment electronically must access the meeting using the Webex
link above by the beginning of the “Citizen Public Input” portion of the meeting. If an
individual is unable to attend the meeting, they may also email their comments to
councilwebex@slco.org by 10:00 AM the day of the meeting to have those comments
distributed to the Council and read into the record at the appropriate time.
The first time you join via the link may take longer to get through the set-up steps. Please
plan accordingly.
Please include "Resident" ahead of your first name when you join the meeting or you will
not be identified as wanting to give comment.
This website has helpful tips for using Webex for Events:

**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** County internal admission undermining their defense

> *Key Quote:* bject: proposed quarry in Parleys Canyon
Hello Deputy Mayor Kanter, I cover the environment for Salt Lake Tribune and we have a story in the works about a
proposed limestone quarry in Parleys Canyon.

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: "Catherine Kanter" </O=SALT LAKE COUNTY/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE
GROUP
(FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=2FDF5521CFC24EF49092119A1226FE2B

Subject: RE: proposed quarry in Parleys Canyon
Date: Mon, 22 Nov 2021 18:43:02 -0700
Importance: Normal
Inline-Images: image001.png

Hi Brian. Thanks for reaching out. I was not aware of the proposed limestone quarry. Let me touch base with our team
tomorrow and we will coordinate with Parks and Rec as well. I suspect someone will be in touch before your Wednesday
deadline.
Warm regards,
Catherine

SALT LAKE

From: Brian Maffly <bmaffly@sltrib.com>
Sent: Monday, November 22, 2021 4:48 PM
To: Catherine Kanter <CKanter@slco.org>
Subject: proposed quarry in Parleys Canyon
Hello Deputy Mayor Kanter, I cover the environment for Salt Lake Tribune and we have a story in the works about a
proposed limestone quarry in Parleys Canyon. A developer filed a proposal for a substantial operation with DOGM last
week.
We hope to speak with someone from the Salt Lake County mayor's office about potential concerns for such a project
and about what approvals would be required from the county. We have already spoken to Laura Briefer about the city's
concerns.
I have reached out to Patrick Leary and Jordan Carroll, as well, but I thought I should run this by the mayor's office. We
plan to post our story on Wednesday.
Thanks!
--

la

Brian Maffly
Public lands reporter

**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

```
From: Jordan Carroll <JCarroll@slco.org>

Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
Date: Fri, 10 Dec 2021 09:47:30 -0700

Attachments: Mayor_Wilson_Statement_on_Amending_Canyon_Ordinance_Related_to_Mineral_Extracti

Chloe Morroni

cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend Canyon
Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to begin the process to
amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in forestry and
recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is issuing the following
statement:
Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today. The message from
Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the Council, my planning staff, and the
District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the outpouring of public concern about proposed
extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be allowed by
County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious areas, especially as
we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and
safeguard our canyon areas for today and future generations.

###
For those unable to attend the meeting this morning at 9:30 a.m., a livestream is available on the County Council’s
Facebook page and the meeting agenda/attachments are located here.

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
Office of Regional Development

beauty and accessibility with something like this proposed open limestone quarry.
I am sure you are a

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
FILED
JANUARY 16 2022
SECRETARY, BOARD OF
OIL, GAS & MINING
Julie Carter <juliecarter@utah.gov>

Parleys Canyon
Emily Pulver <epulver14@gmail.com>
To: juliecarter@utah.gov

Sun, Jan 16, 2022 at 8:21 AM

Julie,
I am writing with my concerns about the proposed quarry mine in Parleys Canyon. We have a family
cabin in Mt. Aire and know other friends and family members that also have cabins there. It is a
beautiful spot we love to enjoy. Not only do we enjoy it but thousands of other people do as well.
That area is used for a lot of recreation by many people. It's also used by thousands each day for
transportation.
There are also concerns impacting wildlife, water and air quality, and traffic, to name a few. Many
people come from all over the world to see this area of Utah and it would be a shame to cloud the
beauty and accessibility with something like this proposed open limestone quarry.
I am sure you are aware of these negative effects so my main purpose in this email is to provide you
with one more family who has worries and concerns, not only for ourselves and how it impacts just
us, but for the community and all the people that it would negatively impact.
Thank you for your time and consideration,
Emily Pulver

To whom it may concern:
On January 26, 2022, the Division of Oil, Gas and Mining (Division) received an Amended Notice of Intention
to Commence Large Mining Operations (Notice) for the 1-80 South Quarry (formally Silver Mine by Tree Farms
LLC). This amendment updates contact information to the new operator Granite Construction. Please be aware
that because this plan is not approved, the Division cannot approve this amendment.
There are still several outstanding deficiencies from the last review that need to be address prior to approval.
Therefore, the Division is returning this amendment. With any new responses or amendment please make sure
that this amendment is incorporated into the plan and that Granite Construction signs future submittals including
the mine signature page.
All future correspondence should reference M/035/0054. Thank you for your help in keeping this permit current.

Upon request and with three working days’ notice, Salt Lake County will provide free auxiliary
aids and services to qualified individuals (including sign language interpreters, alternative formats,
etc.). For assistance, please call (385) 468-7500 – TTY 711.
Members of the Council may participate electronically. Meetings may be closed for reasons
allowed by statute. Motions relating to any of the items listed below, including final action, may
be taken.
This meeting will be simulcast electronically via Webex Events. Agendas, audio
live-streams and recordings, and meeting minutes can be accessed at slco.legistar.com. The
Council will also broadcast live-streams of its meetings on Facebook Live, which may be
accessed at http://www.facebook.com/slcocouncil/, and through Cisco Webex, which may
be accessed at:
https://slco.webex.com/slco/onstage/g.php?MTID=ec58d0e1961b33a1c06b89ff9083f82b7
Individuals wishing to comment electronically must access the meeting using the Webex
link above by the beginning of the “Citizen Public Input” portion of the meeting. If an
individual is unable to attend the meeting, they may also email their comments to
councilwebex@slco.org by 10:00 AM the day of the meeting to have those comments
distributed to the Council and read into the record at the appropriate time.
The first time you join via the link may take longer to get through the set-up steps. Please
plan accordingly.
Please include "Resident" ahead of your first name when you join the meeting or you will
not be identified as wanting to give comment.
This website has helpful tips for using Webex for Events:
https://help.webex.com/ld-7srxjs-CiscoWebexEvents/Webex-Events

### SLCo011005 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

SLC_5827020.1

### SLCo011022 — SIM GILL
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* drafted if the County elects to do so. As a point of information,
following the public hearing on April 5, 2022, the County Council voted unanimously to advance the
amendments, and did so based on una

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
SIM GILL

Ralph Chamness

DISTRICT ATTORNEY

Chief Deputy
Civil Division

Jeffrey William Hall
Chief Deputy
Justice Division

Blake Nakamura

Lisa Ashman

Chief Deputy
Justice Division

Administrative
Operations

April 7, 2022
Via email – jcullimore@utah.gov
Utah Office of the Property Rights Ombudsman
Attn: Jordan Cullimore
Re: Tree Farm Request for Mediation
Dear Jordan:
As a follow up to our conversation last week, I write to address the issues raised by Tree Farm, LLC (TF)
in its letter and request for mediation (Request) filed with your office. In the Request, TF asserts that a
proposed amendment to the Salt Lake County zoning code has already imposed a regulatory taking on
TF. Then, based on the County’s proposed legislative amendments to its land use code, TF asserts that it
is entitled to just compensation from Salt Lake County. These assertions are not supported by the law.
Utah Code § 13-43-204 provides that the Ombudsman’s office can mediate disputes involving takings or
eminent domain issues. However, subsection (3)(b) of this section provides that mediation is not
appropriate if, in the opinion of the Property Rights Ombudsman, the issues are not ripe for review, no
cause of action exists (assuming the alleged facts are true), all issues raised are beyond the scope of the
Ombudsman’s statutory duty to review, or the mediation is otherwise not appropriate. For the following
reasons, mediation at this time is not appropriate under this statute.
In his letter, Mr. Bateman asserts that the County is prohibited from adopting or amending ordinances that
prohibit operations that remove “sand, gravel, and rock aggregate,” which are critical infrastructure
materials as defined by Utah Code §§ 17-27a-1001 & 17-41-101. As grounds, Mr. Bateman cited Utah
Code § 17-41-406(6), which limits the County’s ability to amend its existing land use ordinances to
prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical infrastructure materials operations. However, the
proposed amendments do not include any reference to critical infrastructure materials or critical
infrastructure materials operations, as defined by those statutes. As such, the proposed changes do not
conflict with Utah Code § 17-41-406, and the County is legally entitled to move forward with the
proposed amendments as currently drafted if the County elects to do so. As a point of information,
following the public hearing on April 5, 2022, the County Council voted unanimously to advance the
amendments, and did so based on unanimous public comment in support. The proposed amendments are
enclosed with this letter.
Second, TF claims that because Salt Lake County has initiated proceedings to amend its Forest Recreation
(FR)and Foothills Canyons Overlay Zone (FCOZ) zoning regulations to eliminate “mineral extraction” as
a conditional use within those zones, TF purportedly has suffered a regulatory taking. However, a
regulatory taking claim is not ripe until a government entity has issued a “fina
... [truncated — full text is 4415 characters]
```

Date: Fri, 10 Dec 2021 09:47:30 -0700

Chloe Morroni

cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend Canyon
Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to begin the process to
amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in forestry and
recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is issuing the following
statement:
Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today. The message from
Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the Council, my planning staff, and the
District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the outpouring of public concern about proposed
extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be allowed by
County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious areas, especially as
we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and
safeguard our canyon areas for today and future generations.

###
For those unable to attend the meeting this morning at 9:30 a.m., a livestream is available on the County Council’s
Facebook page and the meeting agenda/attachments are located here.

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend
Canyon Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to
begin the process to amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing
as a conditional use in forestry and recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is

Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today.

Council, my planning staff, and the District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the
outpouring of public concern about proposed extraction operations.

allowed by County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious
areas, especially as we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my
administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and safeguard our canyon areas for today and future
generations.

Julie,
I am writing with my concerns about the proposed quarry mine in Parleys Canyon. We have a family

### SLCo015177 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* purpose
of my letter is to make you aware that any attempts to do so will be a violation of state law. In
addition, be aware that my client currently has a vested critical infrastructure materials op

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

February 11, 2022
Via – zshaw@slco.org
Zachary D. Shaw
Salt Lake County Deputy District Attorney
35 East 500 South
Salt Lake City, Utah 84111
Dear Mr. Shaw:
Be advised that this law firm represents Tree Farm, LLC. It has come to my attention that Salt
Lake County is currently preparing ordinances to restrict the mining and extraction of critical
infrastructure materials from various properties my client owns in Parleys Canyon. The purpose
of my letter is to make you aware that any attempts to do so will be a violation of state law. In
addition, be aware that my client currently has a vested critical infrastructure materials operation
on the property.
Utah Code 17-41-402(6) reads:
(6)
(a)

(b)

A county, city, or town may not:
adopt, enact, or amend an existing land use regulation, ordinance, or
regulation that would prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical
infrastructure materials operations, including vested critical infrastructure
materials operations as defined in Section 10-9a-901 or 17-27a-001; or
initiate proceedings to amend the county's, city's, or town's land use
ordinances as described in Subsection 10-9a-509(1)(a)(ii) or 17-27a508(1)(a)(ii).

Accordingly, under this section of the Utah State Code, Salt Lake County cannot enact or even
initiate proceedings to enact ordinances that restrict or prohibit critical infrastructure materials
operations. There are no qualifiers to this plain language. Thus, Salt Lake County cannot legally
adopt new ordinances that will restrict extraction of critical infrastructure materials on my client’s
property.
Moreover, the definition of vested critical infrastructure materials operation in Utah Code 10-9a901(4) reads thus:
(4)

"Vested critical infrastructure materials operations" means critical
infrastructure materials operations operating in accordance with a legal
nonconforming use or a permit issued by the municipality that existed or

via email

RE: Mediation/Arbitration Request: Tree Farm, LLC
Property Address: 4402 East I-80 (Parley’s Canyon)
Dear Ms. Hobbs:
Attached please find a request for mediation that the Office of the Property Rights
Ombudsman (the “Office”) has received from Brent N. Bateman, on behalf of Tree Farm,
LLC (“Tree Farm”). The issue relates to action by Salt Lake County (“SLCO”). The Office
has reviewed the request and believes that it raises issues that may be appropriate for
mediation and/or arbitration under Utah statute. (See Utah Code § 13-43-204.)
According to the information we have received, Mr. Bateman indicates that Tree Farm is
mining and extracting critical infrastructure materials from various properties, owned by
Tree Farm, in Parley’s Canyon. Mr. Bateman claims SLCO is considering and has recently
passed zoning legislation to restrict further mining and extraction. Mr. Bateman asserts
that the County’s actions amount to a regulatory taking of his client’s property without
compensation. Tree Farm is seeking mediation to resolve this dispute.
We would like to proceed to have an initial conversation on the matter as soon as possible
to gather the perspectives of the other parties involved. In the interim, please consider
the following issues and respond if necessary.
* Are the facts as alleged true?
* Is there a chance to settle this matter without formal arbitration?
* Are there reasons that you believe this matter is not ripe for review?

160 East 300 South, PO Box 146702, Salt Lake City, UT 84114-6702• telephone (801) 530-6391 • propertyrights.utah.gov

March 23, 2022
Page 2 of 2
* Is this dispute, or part of it, beyond the scope of this Office’s right to provide for
mediation or arbitration under the statute?
* Is the matter inappropriate for mediation or arbitration based on some other
factors?
Our Office would be eager to assist in any meaningful way with efforts to resolve the
matter in the most informal and expeditious manner possible, so long as this does not
result in unreasonable delay or other unfairness.
The attorneys in the Office are available to serve as the arbitrator in this matter. We are
also willing to assist as mediators if we can resolve the issues without arbitration. If

accommodated.

March 23, 2022

Rashelle Hobbs, City Recorder
Salt Lake County
2001 South State St. N1-600
Salt Lake City, Utah 84190

via email

RE: Mediation/Arbitration Request: Tree Farm, LLC
Property Address: 4402 East I-80 (Parley’s Canyon)
Dear Ms. Hobbs:
Attached please find a request for mediation that the Office of the Property Rights
Ombudsman (the “Office”) has received from Brent N. Bateman, on behalf of Tree Farm,
LLC (“Tree Farm”). The issue relates to action by Salt Lake County (“SLCO”). The Office
has reviewed the request and believes that it raises issues that may be appropriate for
mediation and/or arbitration under Utah statute. (See Utah Code § 13-43-204.)
According to the information we have received, Mr. Bateman indicates that Tree Farm is
mining and extracting critical infrastructure materials from various properties, owned by
Tree Farm, in Parley’s Canyon. Mr. Bateman claims SLCO is considering and has recently
passed zoning legislation to restrict further mining and extraction. Mr. Bateman asserts
that the County’s actions amount to a regulatory taking of his client’s property without
compensation. Tree Farm is seeking mediation to resolve this dispute.
We would like to proceed to have an initial conversation on the matter as soon as possible
to gather the perspectives of the other parties involved. In the interim, please consider
the following issues and respond if necessary.
* Are the facts as alleged true?
* Is there a chance to settle this matter without formal arbitration?
* Are there reasons that you believe this matter is not ripe for review?

160 East 300 South, PO Box 146702, Salt Lake City, UT 84114-6702• telephone (801) 530-6391 • propertyrights.utah.gov

Rashelle Hobbs
March 23, 2022
Page 2 of 2
* Is this dispute, or part of it, beyond the scope of this Office’s right to provide for
mediation or arbitration under the statute?
* Is the matter inappropriate for mediation or arbitration based on some other
factors?
Our Office would be eager to assist in any meaningful way with efforts to resolve the
matter in the most informal and expeditious manner possible, so long as this does not
result in unreasonable delay or other unfairness.
The attorneys in the Office are available to serve as the arbitrator in this matter. We are
also willing to assist as mediators if we can resolve the issues without arbitration. If
requested, a need for remote mediation through video conferencing can be
accommodated.
Thank you for your attention to this matter. Please advise me of any questions or
suggestions you have.
Sincerely,

Jordan S. Cullimore
Lead Attorney

### SLCo015521 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
SIM GILL

Ralph Chamness

Blake Nakamura

April 7, 2022
Via email – jcullimore@utah.gov
Utah Office of the Property Rights Ombudsman
Attn: Jordan Cullimore
Re: Tree Farm Request for Mediation
Dear Jordan:
As a follow up to our conversation last week, I write to address the issues raised by Tree Farm, LLC (TF)
in its letter and request for mediation (Request) filed with your office. In the Request, TF asserts that a
proposed amendment to the Salt Lake County zoning code has already imposed a regulatory taking on
TF. Then, based on the County’s proposed legislative amendments to its land use code, TF asserts that it
is entitled to just compensation from Salt Lake County. These assertions are not supported by the law.
Utah Code § 13-43-204 provides that the Ombudsman’s office can mediate disputes involving takings or
eminent domain issues. However, subsection (3)(b) of this section provides that mediation is not
appropriate if, in the opinion of the Property Rights Ombudsman, the issues are not ripe for review, no
cause of action exists (assuming the alleged facts are true), all issues raised are beyond the scope of the
Ombudsman’s statutory duty to review, or the mediation is otherwise not appropriate. For the following
reasons, mediation at this time is not appropriate under this statute.
In his letter, Mr. Bateman asserts that the County is prohibited from adopting or amending ordinances that
prohibit operations that remove “sand, gravel, and rock aggregate,” which are critical infrastructure
materials as defined by Utah Code §§ 17-27a-1001 & 17-41-101. As grounds, Mr. Bateman cited Utah
Code § 17-41-406(6), which limits the County’s ability to amend its existing land use ordinances to
prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical infrastructure materials operations. However, the
proposed amendments do not include any reference to critical infrastructure materials or critical
infrastructure materials operations, as defined by those statutes. As such, the proposed changes do not
conflict with Utah Code § 17-41-406, and the County is legally entitled to move forward with the
proposed amendments as currently drafted if the County elects to do so. As a point of information,
following the public hearing on April 5, 2022, the County Council voted unanimously to advance the
amendments, and did so based on unanimous public comment in support. The proposed amendments are
enclosed with this letter.
Second, TF claims that because Salt Lake County has initiated proceedings to amend its Forest Recreation
(FR)and Foothills Canyons Overlay Zone (FCOZ) zoning regulations to eliminate “mineral extraction” as
a conditional use within those zones, TF purportedly has suffered a regulatory taking. However, a
regulatory taking claim is not ripe until a government entity has issued a “fina
... [truncated — full text is 4415 characters]
```

### SLCo015544 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Brent N. Bateman

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.

Salt Lake County Deputy District Attorney
35 East 500 South
Salt Lake City, Utah 84111
Dear Mr. Shaw:
Be advised that this law firm represents Tree Farm, LLC. It has come to my attention that Salt
Lake County is currently preparing ordinances to restrict the mining and extraction of critical
infrastructure materials from various properties my client owns in Parleys Canyon. The purpose
of my letter is to make you aware that any attempts to do so will be a violation of state law. In
addition, be aware that my client currently has a vested critical infrastructure materials operation
on the property.
Utah Code 17-41-402(6) reads:
(6)
(a)

(b)

A county, city, or town may not:
adopt, enact, or amend an existing land use regulation, ordinance, or
regulation that would prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical
infrastructure materials operations, including vested critical infrastructure
materials operations as defined in Section 10-9a-901 or 17-27a-001; or
initiate proceedings to amend the county's, city's, or town's land use
ordinances as described in Subsection 10-9a-509(1)(a)(ii) or 17-27a508(1)(a)(ii).

Accordingly, under this section of the Utah State Code, Salt Lake County cannot enact or even
initiate proceedings to enact ordinances that restrict or prohibit critical infrastructure materials
operations. There are no qualifiers to this plain language. Thus, Salt Lake County cannot legally
adopt new ordinances that will restrict extraction of critical infrastructure materials on my client’s
property.
Moreover, the definition of vested critical infrastructure materials operation in Utah Code 10-9a901(4) reads thus:
(4)

"Vested critical infrastructure materials operations" means critical
infrastructure materials operations operating in accordance with a legal
nonconforming use or a permit issued by the municipality that existed or

Attached please find a request for mediation that the Office of the Property Rights

LLC (“Tree Farm”). The issue relates to action by Salt Lake County (“SLCO”). The Office
has reviewed the request and believes that it raises issues that may be appropriate for
mediation and/or arbitration under Utah statute. (See Utah Code § 13-43-204.)
According to the information we have received, Mr. Bateman indicates that Tree Farm is
mining and extracting critical infrastructure materials from various properties, owned by
Tree Farm, in Parley’s Canyon. Mr. Bateman claims SLCO is considering and has recently
passed zoning legislation to restrict further mining and extraction. Mr. Bateman asserts
that the County’s actions amount to a regulatory taking of his client’s property without

the following issues and respond if necessary.
* Are the facts as alleged true?
* Is there a chance to settle this matter without formal arbitration?
* Are there reasons that you believe this matter is not ripe for review?

### SLCo015585 — Planning Commission Chairman - Opening Statement
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claim 5 only | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** County internal admission undermining their defense

> *Key Quote:* n - Opening Statement
Updated January 22, 2013
To be read at the opening of the public hearing item portion of the agenda.
A copy of today's agenda and a sign-in sheet are located on a stand at the ba

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Planning Commission Chairman - Opening Statement
Updated January 22, 2013
To be read at the opening of the public hearing item portion of the agenda.
A copy of today's agenda and a sign-in sheet are located on a stand at the back of the room.
Please note your participation in today's meeting by signing in.
The Planning Commission is a voluntary citizen board. The Commission's function is to hear
and decide applications for conditional uses and preliminary subdivision plats; and to make
recommendations to the County Council for zoning changes or changes to ordinances or general
plans.
The agenda is divided into two main categories: Public Hearing Items and Business Items.
At this time we will begin the Public Hearing portion of the agenda. These items are ones for
which public comment is taken so that the Planning Commission can be made aware of all of the
issues of concern with regards to a request. Decisions may be made on any item listed on the
agenda. A decision, or recommendation, will be rendered by the Planning Commission for these
items which may include Approval, Approval with Conditions, Denial, or, Continuation of the
item to a future meeting.
The Commissions decisions are based on: information from field observations;
recommendations from Planning Staff and other agencies, regarding compliance with the general
plan and relevant ordinances; the Community Council recommendation as a representation of
community concerns; and information presented at the public meeting, including a presentation
by the applicant and testimony from the public.
Today's meeting is recorded, so please speak directly into the microphone, and state your
name and address prior to making your comments. Please note that comments from the
audience are only appropriate when presented at the podium.
The meeting will proceed as outlined in the Rules of Conduct printed on the back of the agenda.
To be read at the opening of the business item portion of the agenda.
At this time will proceed with the Business portion of the Commission's Agenda.
As stated earlier today, The Planning Commission is a voluntary citizen board. The
Commission's function is to hear and decide applications for conditional uses and preliminary
subdivision plats; and to make recommendations to the County Council for zoning changes or
changes to ordinances or general plans.
This portion of today's meeting is dedicated to Business Items. Members of the public may
attend, but will not participate unless invited to do so by the Chair or supporting staff.
During this time the Commission may discuss and render decisions on policy issues and
administrative matters that do not require public input. Special presentations, reports, and
updates from the supporting staff that do not require a decision at a Public Hearing may also be
made. There will be no discussion of an application, request, or approval scheduled for the
Public Hearing Item portion of the meeting.

Rules of Conduct for the Planning Commissio
... [truncated — full text is 4065 characters]
```
