### SLCo015681 — December 10, 2021
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 3, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** County internal admission undermining their defense

> *Key Quote:* or Wilson is
issuing the following statement:

Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today.
The message from Salt Lake County is clear: we will

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
December 10, 2021
Contact:

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
jcarroll@slco.org
(385) 479-2086

Chloe Morroni
Communications Director
cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend
Canyon Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to
begin the process to amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing
as a conditional use in forestry and recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is
issuing the following statement:

Salt Lake County prioritizes our environment and recreation, and we demonstrated those values today.
The message from Salt Lake County is clear: we will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the
Council, my planning staff, and the District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the
outpouring of public concern about proposed extraction operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not be
allowed by County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s precious
areas, especially as we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my
administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and safeguard our canyon areas for today and future
generations.

###


```

### SLCo016926 — Proposed mining in Parley's Canyon
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* cles traveling on it, and nearby buildings and residences. Will it
again become environmentally friendly? Will those who mined the gravel revegetate and restore what's left? We
certainly need to addre

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: Bill Hanson <william.f.hanson@gmail.com>
To: LLStringham@slco.org, RSnelgrove@slco.org, JBradley@slco.org, DHTheodore@slco.org
Subject: Proposed mining in Parley's Canyon
Date: Mon, 04 Apr 2022 12:09:14 -0600
Importance: Normal

My name is William (Bill) F. Hanson. I've lived in Salt Lake County all my life, and have traveled up and down
Parleys Canyon countless times. I personally know Jim Bradley, although I haven't seen him for some time, and
Dea Theordore, a neighbor of mine. I think both can vouch that I'm not unreasonable. I've hiked all over the
Wasatch Range, and, even though I'm an old guy, still do so. The Wasatch Range is a great treasure that should
not be damaged by a mine in Parley's Canyon. These are some of the many reasons why.
1. Parley's Canyon is the primary means by which eastbound and westbound traffic enters and leaves the Salt
Lake Valley. As we all know, it's a lovely green in the Spring and Summer, yellow and red in the Fall, and white
in the Winter. It's a beautiful canyon that we all love and enjoy and an impressive way to enter and exit the Salt
Lake Valley. A huge strip-mine scar on its south side would irretrievably damage its beauty, all because some
guy wants to make lots of money at the expense of those of us who treasure it and live in the Salt Lake Valley.
2. As we who live in the Salt Lake Valley know, Winter inversions plague our air quality. And, even in other
seasons, the Salt Lake Valley's air quality can rapidly deteriorate. A huge gravel strip mine in Parley's Canyon,
together with its heavy machinery and gravel-hauling trucks, would, in my view, drastically exacerbate the
Valley's air quality, particularly in the Winter months, as strong winds typically blow down the Canyon. Will the
owner of the mine compensate those who suffer from the resulting dirty air and pay for the measures to clean it?
3. Parley's Canyon is, as a major east-west interstate traffic artery, well-traveled. As we know, it sometimes
suffers from heavily-congested heavy traffic, particularly during rush-hour times and when a vehicular accident
slows traffic to a crawl. A fleet of heavy gravel trucks, which will be needed to haul gravel up and down the
canyon from the proposed mine, will vastly exacerbate traffic congestion in the canyon. Moreover, those trucks
will, unless meticulously sealed, will spew gravel over other vehicles on the road. Will the owner of the
proposed mine willingly cover damage to other vehicles resulting from loose gravel? And, the constant use of
heavy trucks will cause the Parley's Canyon road to deteriorate much sooner than it otherwise would. Will the
owner of the proposed mine pay additional highway taxes commensurate with that deterioration? .
4. We've all seen what has happened to what used to be the Point of the Mountain. Heavy gravel mining there
has leveled the western part of it to the extent that there's no point left. Moreover, on windy days, gravel dust
from the mine can cover both the Inte
... [truncated — full text is 3658 characters]
```

### SLCo017173 — Date:
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
Count

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

Durham Jones & Pinegar ► LEAD Advogados ► Rattagan Macchiavello Arocena ► Jiménez de Aréchaga Viana & Brause ► Lee International ►
Kensington Swan ► Bingham Greenebaum ► Cohen & Grigsby ► Sayarh & Menjra ► Larraín Rencoret ► For more information on the firms that
have come together to form Dentons, go to dentons.com/legacyfirms
Dentons is an international legal practice providing client services worldwide through its member firms and affiliates. Please see dentons.com for Legal Notices.

Brent N. Bateman

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043

dentons.com

April 5, 2022
Via – councilwebex@slco.org
Salt Lake County Council
2001 South State Street N2-200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84114-4575
RE: Public Comment – Ordinance to Eliminate Mineral Extraction
Dear Salt Lake County Council:
I represent Tree Farm, LLC, and submit this comment on my client’s behalf.
I have made multiple efforts over the past several weeks to engage with Salt Lake County regarding the
proposed ordinance to eliminate mineral extraction and processing as a conditional use in the Forestry
and Recreation Zone. With the exception of some very summary and dismissive emails from County
Attorney Zach Shaw, my efforts have largely been ignored. Noting that this matter is again on the County
Council Agenda for today (April 5, 2022), I hereby submit this letter as my public comment for this
meeting.
This ordinance is blatantly contrary to Utah Code 17-41-402(6). This law prohibits adopting or initiating
proceedings to adopt any ordinance that would prohibit Critical Infrastructure Materials operations. As you
are aware, "Critical infrastructure materials" means sand, gravel, or rock aggregate. Utah Code 10-9a901(1). Although I have pointed this out, no one at the County has bothered to explain to me how this
ordinance complies with this state code section. My only guess to justify this ordinance is that it is styled
“an ordinance prohibiting mineral extraction” rather than prohibiting extraction of critical infrastructure
materials. However, this justification fails because the text of the ordinance expressly prohibits extraction
of “sand, gravel and/or rock aggregate.” Thus, where it was not prohibited before, this ordinance clearly
prohibits critical infrastructure materials. Thus, it is illegal.
This ordinance will affect the property rights of not only my client, but of many others. I hope that the
County will press pause and engage in some discussions about this matter. I further hope that it is not the
County’s conscious intention to disobey state law. Thank you for considering my comment.
Very truly yours,
DENTONS DURHAM JONES PINEGAR P.C.

Brent N. Bateman

### SLCo018477 — Brent N. Bateman
**Element:** A-Rebut Zoning Power | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence county exceeded its zoning authority / state preemption

> *Key Quote:* purpose
of my letter is to make you aware that any attempts to do so will be a violation of state law. In
addition, be aware that my client currently has a vested critical infrastructure materials op

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Brent N. Bateman
Attorney at Law
brent.bateman@dentons.com
D 1+ (801) 375-6600

Dentons Durham Jones Pinegar P.C.
3301 N. Thanksgiving Way, Suite 400
Lehi, Utah 84043
United States
dentons.com

February 11, 2022
Via – zshaw@slco.org
Zachary D. Shaw
Salt Lake County Deputy District Attorney
35 East 500 South
Salt Lake City, Utah 84111
Dear Mr. Shaw:
Be advised that this law firm represents Tree Farm, LLC. It has come to my attention that Salt
Lake County is currently preparing ordinances to restrict the mining and extraction of critical
infrastructure materials from various properties my client owns in Parleys Canyon. The purpose
of my letter is to make you aware that any attempts to do so will be a violation of state law. In
addition, be aware that my client currently has a vested critical infrastructure materials operation
on the property.
Utah Code 17-41-402(6) reads:
(6)
(a)

(b)

A county, city, or town may not:
adopt, enact, or amend an existing land use regulation, ordinance, or
regulation that would prohibit, restrict, regulate, or otherwise limit critical
infrastructure materials operations, including vested critical infrastructure
materials operations as defined in Section 10-9a-901 or 17-27a-001; or
initiate proceedings to amend the county's, city's, or town's land use
ordinances as described in Subsection 10-9a-509(1)(a)(ii) or 17-27a508(1)(a)(ii).

Accordingly, under this section of the Utah State Code, Salt Lake County cannot enact or even
initiate proceedings to enact ordinances that restrict or prohibit critical infrastructure materials
operations. There are no qualifiers to this plain language. Thus, Salt Lake County cannot legally
adopt new ordinances that will restrict extraction of critical infrastructure materials on my client’s
property.
Moreover, the definition of vested critical infrastructure materials operation in Utah Code 10-9a901(4) reads thus:
(4)

"Vested critical infrastructure materials operations" means critical
infrastructure materials operations operating in accordance with a legal
nonconforming use or a permit issued by the municipality that existed or

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
December 10, 2021
Contact:

Jordan Carroll
Communications Manager
jcarroll@slco.org
(385) 479-2086

Chloe Morroni
Communications Director
cmorroni@slco.org
(385) 261-9301

Mayor Wilson Releases Statement on Salt Lake County’s Decision to Amend
Canyon Ordinance Related to Mineral Extraction
SALT LAKE COUNTY – On Friday, December 10 Salt Lake County Council voted in a special meeting to
begin the process to amend a section of the County code to eliminate mineral extraction and processing
as a conditional use in forestry and recreation zones.
Following the action Mayor Wilson’s administration and County Council have taken, Mayor Wilson is
issuing the following statement:
“Salt Lake County’s values of prioritizing our environment and recreation were manifest today. The
message from Salt Lake County is clear: We will fight to protect our canyons. I want to thank the
Council, my planning staff and the District Attorney for their swift action today and acknowledge the
outpouring of public concern regarding proposed extractive operations.
Creating new mining or extraction operations in our critical wildland-urban interface areas should not
be allowed by County ordinance.
My priority is to support recreation, clean air and water, and the preservation of our canyon’s
precious areas, especially as we see increased demand for use. The County's actions today further my
administration’s ongoing efforts to manage and safeguard our canyon areas for today and future
generations.

Working toward more inclusive & accessible RFAs
Introduction
The Diversity & Inclusion Office reached out to Contracts & Procurement last fall. Together, they convened a
workgroup with ORD, ODI, and IT to focus on reviewing RFA procedures and opportunities to improve
inclusivity, diversity, equity, and accessibility.
Challenges
• RFA process often challenging to navigate for community-based organizations
• The process is decentralized by design (a good thing!), but this impedes sharing lessons learned / best
practices across departments
• Room for improvement on diversity in RFA applicants, especially in recruiting new applicants
Workgroup’s objectives
• Create a community where people can seek help, share expertise, and test new strategies
• Share RFA best practices widely
• Introduce standards for documenting RFA experiences and lessons learned so that this knowledge lives
beyond the person who ran the RFA
• Maintain relationships with community partners, especially partnerships established during COVID
What we’ve done
• Collected common practices on RFA procedures across agencies under the Mayor’s Portfolio
o Developed RFA best practices slide deck
o Identified areas for learning and collaboration opportunities
• Assessed accessibility elements of applications and policies
o Introduced plain language reviews before RFAs posted (piloting with ORD)
o Evaluated ease of use for technical platforms
o Reviewed PDF compliance and taught people how to make PDFs accessib

**Element:** B-Rebut Health/Safety Pretext | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 4, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence that health/safety justification was pretextual / politically motivated

> *Key Quote:* ars ago. Each winter the canyon has at least one small avalanche. We
have grave concerns with how the blasting from the proposed mine will affect the avalanche
conditions in our canyon. We understand

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: Jenny Wilson <JWilson@slco.org>
To: The McGuire Family <jasonmcguire@comcast.net>
Cc: Lisa Hartman <LHartman@slco.org>
Subject: Re: Proposed Parley's Canyon Quarry
Date: Wed, 01 Dec 2021 16:58:28 -0700
Importance: Normal

Hi Jason and Angela,
Thank you for reaching out! As you’re well aware, this is a complex issue that my team is working through. I’m copying
Lisa Hartman, Associate Deputy Mayor. She works with Deputy Mayor Catherine Kanter on this issue because it falls in
their portfolio of regional operations, but also because Lisa serves as the city liaison for me to South Jordan City.

signature_38471

Mayor Jenny Wilson

2001 South State Street

(385) 468-7000

From: The McGuire Family <jasonmcguire@comcast.net>
Date: Monday, November 29, 2021 at 8:08 PM
To: Jenny Wilson <JWilson@slco.org>
Subject: Proposed Parley's Canyon Quarry

Dear Mayor Wilson,
Thank you for all that you do for our County. I serve with Mayor Ramsey on the South Jordan
City Council and she said this was the best way to contact you. My wife and I are contacting you
regarding the proposed Parley’s Canyon Quarry. We have family property and cabins in the
adjacent Mt. Aire Canyon. The Mt. Aire Canyon is a very narrow canyon with a one lane road
and historic cabins that in some places scale the mountain side. The area is prone to
avalanches. Our property in particular has the remains of a historic cabin that was destroyed by
an avalanche many years ago. Each winter the canyon has at least one small avalanche. We
have grave concerns with how the blasting from the proposed mine will affect the avalanche
conditions in our canyon. We understand from the Salt Lake Tribune’s article that you also are
concerned with the impacts that such a business would have to Parley’s canyon. Per the Salt
Lake Tribune’s November 24th article, it states that “The mine would require a conditional use
permit from the county and would have to be reviewed for compliance with the county’s
Foothills and Canyon Overlay Zone ordinance.”
We are trying to understand how the county will be involved in the process of the potential
approval of the Tree Farm LLC. permit. Will the permit be issued solely by the Department

responsible for compliance? Will Tree Farm LLC. have to get your approval as mayor? Does
Tree Farm LLC. have the right to request a variance? Will the permit request go before the
County Council? Will there be opportunities for public input? Please help us to understand the
political process involved with this issue.
We really appreciate all that you do!
Sincerely,
Jason and Angela McGuire
South Jordan City, UT
(801) 703-7801


```

NOTICE OF INTENTION TO COMMENCE LARGE MINING OPERATIONS
The informational requirements in this form are based on provisions of the Mined Land
Reclamation Act, Title 40-8, Utah Code Annotated 1953, General Rules and Rules of Practice and
Procedures.
This form applies only to mining operations which disturb or will disturb more than five
acres in an incorporated area or ten acres in an unincorporated area at any given time.
"MINING OPERATIONS" means those activities conducted on the surface of the land for the exploration
for, development of, or extraction of a mineral deposit, including, but not limited to, surface mining and
the surface effects of underground and in situ mining, on-site transportation, concentrating, milling,
evaporation, and other primary processing.
"Mining operation" does not include: the extraction of sand, gravel, and rock aggregate; the extraction of
oil and gas as defined in Chapter 6, Title 40; the extraction of geothermal steam; smelting or refining
operations; off-site operations and transportation; or reconnaissance activities which will not cause
significant surface resource disturbance or involve the use of mechanized earth-moving equipment such
as bulldozers or backhoes.

### SLCo011350 — RE: Meeting Request
**Element:** B-Rebut Health/Safety Pretext | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence that health/safety justification was pretextual / politically motivated

> *Key Quote:* arry planned for
Parleys Canyon. This started the process to amend the county’s zoning ordinances to prohibit new quarries from being
developed in the Wasatch foothills. There is concern that this may

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: Christie Morgan <CMorgan@slco.org>
To: Aimee Winder Newton <ANewton@slco.org>
Subject: RE: Meeting Request
Date: Fri, 18 Feb 2022 12:57:11 -0700
Importance: Normal
Inline-Images: image001.png

This is in regard to the special session back in December that was the first step to block a limestone quarry planned for
Parleys Canyon. This started the process to amend the county’s zoning ordinances to prohibit new quarries from being
developed in the Wasatch foothills. There is concern that this may conflict with a law passed in 2019 prohibiting counties
from restricting the extraction of aggregate and other “critical infrastructure materials.”
A company called Tree Farm wants to use drills and heavy explosives in Parleys Canyon near Grandeur Peak to pull out 2
million tons of crushed limestone each year. Tree Farm is a Utah company registered to developer Jesse Lassley, who
previously owned a home in the neighboring Mt. Aire Canyon. The plan was brought to the council’s attention in
November after the company submitted a notice of intent to the Utah Division of Oil, Gas and Mining.
Homeowners in Mt. Aire Canyon organized an opposition campaign and have a website https://saveparleys.org/
Tree Farm’s application for a small mine was denied, reasoning that the company’s true intent is to develop a large mine,
as opposed to the maximum 20-acre footprint allowed under a small-mine permit.
Tree Farm disputed that decision, and an appeal will be heard Feb. 23. Salt Lake City and Millcreek are asking that Tree
Farm should not be allowed to circumvent the state’s more robust permitting procedure for large mines.
Tree Farm has named Granite Construction as their operator and are calling the location the I-80 South Quarry. They have
a website https://www.i80southquarry.com/
Here are links to a couple of SLTrib articles:
https://www.sltrib.com/news/environment/2021/12/10/salt-lake-county-moves/
https://www.sltrib.com/news/environment/2022/01/29/granite-construction/
Let me know if you’d like more information and I can keep researching!
Christie
From: Aimee Winder Newton <ANewton@slco.org>
Sent: Thursday, February 17, 2022 6:26 PM
To: Christie Morgan <CMorgan@slco.org>
Subject: Re: Meeting Request
Great! Any info you can dig up on this for me so I’m prepared for this meeting would be great!
Aimee Winder Newton
Salt Lake County Council

vulnerability of the foothill and canyon areas to this type of development. We’re relieved that the proposed ordinance
change has been set in motion. But we also have concerns around potential state legislative intervention, among other
concerns. I’d love to learn how Councilwoman Winder Newton thinks about these vul
... [truncated — full text is 4592 characters]

NOTICE OF INTENTION TO COMMENCE LARGE MINING OPERATIONS
The informational requirements in this form are based on provisions of the Mined Land
Reclamation Act, Title 40-8, Utah Code Annotated 1953, General Rules and Rules of Practice and
Procedures.
This form applies only to mining operations which disturb or will disturb more than five
acres in an incorporated area or ten acres in an unincorporated area at any given time.
"MINING OPERATIONS" means those activities conducted on the surface of the land for the exploration
for, development of, or extraction of a mineral deposit, including, but not limited to, surface mining and
the surface effects of underground and in situ mining, on-site transportation, concentrating, milling,
evaporation, and other primary processing.
"Mining operation" does not include: the extraction of sand, gravel, and rock aggregate; the extraction of
oil and gas as defined in Chapter 6, Title 40; the extraction of geothermal steam; smelting or refining
operations; off-site operations and transportation; or reconnaissance activities which will not cause
significant surface resource disturbance or involve the use of mechanized earth-moving equipment such
as bulldozers or backhoes.

### SLCo018527 — Proposed Parley's Canyon Quarry
**Element:** B-Rebut Health/Safety Pretext | **Applies to:** Claims 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 | **SUPPORTS**

**Legal Significance:** Evidence that health/safety justification was pretextual / politically motivated

> *Key Quote:* ars ago. Each winter the canyon has at least one small avalanche. We
have grave concerns with how the blasting from the proposed mine will affect the avalanche
conditions in our canyon. We understand

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
From: "The McGuire Family" <jasonmcguire@comcast.net>
To: "Jenny Wilson" <JWilson@slco.org>
Subject: Proposed Parley's Canyon Quarry
Date: Mon, 29 Nov 2021 20:08:40 -0700
Importance: Normal

Dear Mayor Wilson,
Thank you for all that you do for our County. I serve with Mayor Ramsey on the South Jordan
City Council and she said this was the best way to contact you. My wife and I are contacting you
regarding the proposed Parley’s Canyon Quarry. We have family property and cabins in the
adjacent Mt. Aire Canyon. The Mt. Aire Canyon is a very narrow canyon with a one lane road
and historic cabins that in some places scale the mountain side. The area is prone to
avalanches. Our property in particular has the remains of a historic cabin that was destroyed by
an avalanche many years ago. Each winter the canyon has at least one small avalanche. We
have grave concerns with how the blasting from the proposed mine will affect the avalanche
conditions in our canyon. We understand from the Salt Lake Tribune’s article that you also are
concerned with the impacts that such a business would have to Parley’s canyon. Per the Salt
Lake Tribune’s November 24th article, it states that “The mine would require a conditional use
permit from the county and would have to be reviewed for compliance with the county’s
Foothills and Canyon Overlay Zone ordinance.”
We are trying to understand how the county will be involved in the process of the potential
approval of the Tree Farm LLC. permit. Will the permit be issued solely by the Department
responsible for compliance? Will Tree Farm LLC. have to get your approval as mayor? Does
Tree Farm LLC. have the right to request a variance? Will the permit request go before the
County Council? Will there be opportunities for public input? Please help us to understand the
political process involved with this issue.
We really appreciate all that you do!
Sincerely,
Jason and Angela McGuire
South Jordan City, UT
(801) 703-7801


```
